25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T3ada,<entryFree id="n17211" key="رَابَنِى" type="main">

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَابَنِى</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (T, S, M, &amp;c.,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرِيبُ</foreign>, (M, Mgh, Msb, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَيْبٌ</foreign> (T, M, Mgh, Msb, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) or the latter is a simple subst., (S, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">occasioned in me disquiet, disturbance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">agitation, of mind:</hi> (Ksh and Bd in ii. 1:) [this is the primary signification; (see <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَةٌ</foreign>;) a signification also borne by   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-1" target="أَرَابَنِى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (see the verses of Khálid cited in this paragraph;) whence the other significations here expl. in what follows:] <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">made me to doubt:</hi> (Msb: and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">رَابَهُ</foreign> is expl. in the Mgh:) or <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (a thing, M) <hi rend="ital">caused me to have what is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doubt combined with suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion</hi>]; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-2" target="أَرَابَنِى" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (M, K: in both of which this meaning is indicated, but not expressed:) but the latter is said by Lth to be bad: (T:) or, (T, M, Msb,) accord. to AZ, (T, Msb,) the former signifies <hi rend="ital">he,</hi> (T, M, *) or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi> i. e. his case, (M, * Msb,) <hi rend="ital">made me to know that there was on his part what is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">something occasioning doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doubt combined with suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion</hi>]; (T, M, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">made me to be certain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sure, of it:</hi> (Msb:) and ↓ the latter signifies <hi rend="ital">made me to think that there was in him what is so termed;</hi> (Sb, T, M, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">without my being certain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sure, of it:</hi> (Msb:) [Az says that] these are the right explanations of the two phrases: (T:) [or] the latter signifies also <foreign lang="ar">جَعَلَ فِىَّ الرِّيَبَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he put into me,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">into my mind, doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]; (Sb, M, K; and in a similar manner <foreign lang="ar">أَرَبْتُهُ</foreign> is expl. in the latter;) or <foreign lang="ar">أَوْهَمَنِى الرِّيبَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he made me to think that which occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]: (K: and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">ارابهُ</foreign> is expl. in the Ham p. 363:) and <foreign lang="ar">رِبْتُهُ</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَوْصَلْتُ إِلَيْهِ الرِّيبَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I made doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., or <hi rend="ital">that which occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">to come to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to reach him</hi>]; (K;) [app. <hi rend="ital">by some act;</hi> for it is said that] <foreign lang="ar">رَابَهُ</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَتَاهُ بِرِيبَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he did to him a thing that occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]: (Ham ubi suprà:) or, (K,) accord. to Lh, the Arabs say, (M,) <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى أَمْرُهُ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَرِيبُنِى</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَيْبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَةٌ</foreign>: when they speak allusively [with respect to the cause of doubt &amp;c., not expressing it,] (<foreign lang="ar">إِذَا كَنَوْا</foreign> [misinterpreted in the TA as meaning “ when they affix a pronoun to the verb, ” for the meaning here intended is clearly shown by what follows,]) they prefix <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> [to the verb, saying   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-3" target="أَرَابَ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَرَبْتُ</foreign>, &amp;c., expl. in the latter part of <pb n="1198"/> this paragraph]; and when they do not speak allusively [with respect to the cause of doubt &amp;c., but express it,] (<foreign lang="ar">إِذَا لَمْ يَكْنُوا</foreign>) they reject that letter; but [so accord. to the M, but in the K “ or, ”] it is allowable to say, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-4" target="أَرَابَنِى" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>الأَمْرُ</foreign>; (M, K;) i. e., to prefix the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> when the verb is made trans.: (M:) accord. to As, (T,) <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى</foreign> [signifies <hi rend="ital">he did what made me to doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to have doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c, <hi rend="ital">and what I disliked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hated;</hi> for it] is said of a man when thou seest, on his part, what makes thee to doubt, &amp;c., (<foreign lang="ar">مَا يُرِيبُكَ</foreign>, [or <foreign lang="ar">مَا يَرِيبُكَ</foreign>,]) and what thou dislikest, or hatest: (T, S:) and Hudheyl say,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-5" target="أَرَابَنِى" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (T, S, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">ارابنى أَمْرُهُ</foreign>, as As says on the authority of 'Eesà Ibn-'Omar; (M;) and <foreign lang="ar">رِبْتُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-6" target="اِرْتَبْتُ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I doubted:</hi> (Msb:) accord. to IAth, <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّكُّ</foreign> [an evident mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">رابنى الشَّىْءُ</foreign>] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-7" target="ارابنى" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> both mean <foreign lang="ar">شَكَّكَنِى وَ أَوْهَمَنِى الرِّيبَةَ بِهِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the thing made me to doubt,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">caused me to think that there was that which occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">in it</hi>]; but when you are certain, or sure, of it, you say [only] <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى</foreign>, without [an incipient] <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>: (TA:) accord. to Lth, <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَيْبٌ</foreign>, signifies <hi rend="ital">the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">event,</hi> [app. said only of that which is evil,] <hi rend="ital">betided me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">befell me:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">رَابَنِى أَمْرُهُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">his affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case, brought upon me doubt</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">شَكًّا</foreign> [in the TA <foreign lang="ar">شَرًّا</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">evil</hi>]) <hi rend="ital">and fear.</hi> (T.) It is said in a trad., of Fátimeh, <foreign lang="ar">يَرِيبُنِى مَا يَرِيبُهَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">That displeases and disquiets me which displeases and disquiets her.</hi> (TA.) And in another, respecting a gazelle lying curled in sleep, <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَرِيبُهُ أَحَدٌ بِشَىْءٍ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">No one shall oppose himself to it and disquiet it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disturb it.</hi> (TA.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">مَا رَابَكَ إِلَى قَطْعِهَا</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">What disquieted thee and constrained thee to cut it off?</hi> as Aboo-Moosà thinks the phrase may be read: but see another reading voce <foreign lang="ar">رَابٌ</foreign>. (TA.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">دَعْ مَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَ إِنَّ</foreign>   
      <foreign lang="ar"><ref cref="n17211-8" target="رِيبَةٌ" n="8" type="0" subtype="FTFSOTF" lang="ar" select="n17217"/>يَرِيبُكَ إِلَى مَا لَا يَريبُكَ فَإِنَّ الكَذِبَ </foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الصِّدْقَ طُمَأْنِينَةٌ</foreign>, (Mgh, TA, *) or, as some relate it,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-9" target="يُرِيبُكَ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (TA,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">Leave thou that which causeth thee to doubt,</hi> (Mgh, TA, *) <hi rend="ital">and occasioneth in thee</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الرِّيبَة</foreign>, which originally signifies <hi rend="ital">disquiet,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disturbance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">agitation, of mind,</hi> [and hence <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., and betake thyself <hi rend="ital">to that which will not cause thee to doubt,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">for verily lying is a thing that occasions disquiet of mind,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">and verily veracity is</hi> a thing that occasions <hi rend="ital">tranquillity;</hi>] because the mind is not at rest when it doubts, but becomes tranquil when it is certain, or sure. (Mgh.) And the Hudhalee, (S, TA,) Khálid Ibn-Zuheyr, (TA,) says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَا قَوْمِ مَا لِى وَ أَبَا ذُؤَيْبِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كُنْتُ إِذَا أَتَوْتُهُ مِنْ غَيْبِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَشُمُّ عِطْفِى وَ يَجُرُّ ثَوْبِى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّنِى <ref cref="n17211-10" target="أَرَبْتُهُ" n="10" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>بِرَيْبِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O my people, what aileth me with Aboo-Dhueyb? I was</hi> (<hi rend="ital">such that</hi>) <hi rend="ital">when I came to him after absence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from being absent, he would smell my side,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">my armpit, and pull my garment, as though I disquieted his mind with doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]: (S and TA, in this art. and in art. <foreign lang="ar">بز</foreign>; but in the latter with <foreign lang="ar">يَبُزُّ</foreign> in the place of its syn. <foreign lang="ar">يَجُرُّ</foreign>:) it is said in the L that <foreign lang="ar">اراب</foreign> is trans. and intrans.; and that he who makes it trans. makes it syn. with <foreign lang="ar">رَابَ</foreign>; and thus it is in the saying of Khálid cited above; the last hemistich of which is also related thus: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّنِى قَدْ رِبْتُهُ بِرَيْبِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> but   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-11" target="اراب" n="11" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n17212"/></foreign> when intrans. signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى بِرِيبَةٍ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">he did an act that occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]; like as <foreign lang="ar">أَلَامَ</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى بِمَا يُلَامُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [he did an act for which he was to be blamed]: and agreeably with this signification is expl. the verse ascribed to El-Mutalemmis, or to Beshshár Ibn-Burdeh, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَخُوكَ الَّذِى إِنْ رِبْتَهُ قَالَ إِنَّمَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L><foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-12" target="أَرَبْتُ" n="12" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>وَ إِنْ لَايَنْتَهُ لَانَ جَانِبُهْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Thy brother is he who, if thou make him to doubt,</hi> &amp;c., (or <hi rend="ital">if thou do to him an act occasioning doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., as expl. in the Ham p. 363, where <foreign lang="ar">عَاتَبْتَهُ</foreign> is put in the place of <foreign lang="ar">لَايَنْتَهُ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">says, Only I have done what occasions doubt,</hi> &amp;c.; <hi rend="ital">and if thou act gently with him, becomes gentle</hi>]: thus the verse is correctly related: he who relates it differently, saying <foreign lang="ar">أَرَبْتَ</foreign>, [and thus I find it in two copies of the T,] asserts that <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ رِبْتَهُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">if thou make him of necessity to have doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17211-13" target="اربت" n="13" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [here said in the TA to be “ with damm, ” but this is evidently a mistranscription for “ with fet-h, ” for it cannot mean with damm to the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>, as <foreign lang="ar">أُرِبْتَ</foreign> does not bear an appropriate signification, nor can it mean with damm to the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>, as the explanation relates to the reading of <foreign lang="ar">اربت</foreign> with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>,] means <hi rend="ital">thou hast caused</hi> [me] <hi rend="ital">to think that there was that which occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">when it was not decidedly necessary.</hi> (TA.)    </entryFree>27:T5b8,<entryFree id="n17212" key="اراب" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>4</itype>

                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, as a trans. verb: see 1, in eight places.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  As intrans., it signifies <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, one in whom was something occasioning doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doubt combined with suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion;</hi> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ ذَا رِيبَةِ</foreign>: (Sb, T, S, M:) and <hi rend="ital">he did a thing that occasioned doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.: (As, T:) it is said when one is told something of a person, or thinks it, or imagines it: (Msb:) see 1, in the former half of the paragraph; and also, in three places, in the latter part of the same paragraph. Also <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing, or an affair, or a case,) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, one in which was something occasioning doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.; i. e. <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ ذَا رَيْبٍ</foreign> (T, K) or <foreign lang="ar">ذا رِيبَةٍ</foreign>. (TA.)    </entryFree>2a:T13b8,<entryFree id="n17216" key="رَيْبٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَيْبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is an inf. n. of 1, (T, M, Mgh, Msb, &amp;c.,) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17216-1" target="رِيبَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n17217"/></foreign>, (M, K,) or the latter is a simple subst.: (S, Msb:) the primary signification of the latter [and of the former also when it is used as a simple subst.] is <hi rend="ital">Disquiet, disturbance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">agitation, of mind:</hi> (Ksh and Bd in ii. 1:) [and hence] the former signifies <hi rend="ital">doubt;</hi> (T, S, Msb;) as also ↓ the latter; (S, Mgh;) because doubt disquiets, or disturbs, the mind: (Ksh and Bd ubi suprà, and Mgh:) and <hi rend="ital">opinion;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">ظَنٌّ</foreign>: (Msb:) and ↓ the latter, (S, M, A, Mgh, K,) and the former also, (M, A, K,) <hi rend="ital">doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">تُهَمَةٌ</foreign> (S, M, A, Mgh, K) and <foreign lang="ar">ظِنَّةٌ</foreign>: (M, A, K:) or the former, [and ↓ the latter also,] <hi rend="ital">doubt combined with suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion:</hi> (IAth, TA:) and <hi rend="ital">a thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an event,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a case, that occasions one doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">doubt combined with suspicion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion;</hi> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَا رَابَكَ مِنْ أَمْرٍ</foreign>: (S, TA:) [in this last sense, the latter is the more common: hence,] lying is termed <foreign lang="ar">رِيبَةٌ</foreign> in a trad. cited above: see 1: (Mgh:) the ↓ pl. of the latter is <foreign lang="ar">رِيَبٌ</foreign>. (Msb.) A man, and a thing or an event or a case, is said to be   
      <foreign lang="ar">ذُو <ref cref="n17216-2" target="رِيبَةٍ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">Having in him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, something occasioning doubt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspicion</hi> &amp;c.]. (A.) [<foreign lang="ar">لَا رَيْبَ</foreign> often occurs as meaning <hi rend="ital">There is no doubt; without doubt; undoubtedly.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence, <foreign lang="ar">رَيْبُ الزَّمَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The accidents,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil accidents, of time,</hi> (Ksh and Bd ubi suprà, [in Fleischer's ed. of the latter <foreign lang="ar">رِيَب</foreign>

(T. [This is said in the TA to be tropical; but I do not find <pb n="1199"/> it so characterized in the A.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence, likewise,] <foreign lang="ar">رَيْبٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">A want; a needful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">requisite, thing, affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">business;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">حَاجَةٌ</foreign>.                      <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">قَضَيْنَا مِنْ تِهَامَةَ كُلَّ رَيْبٍ</foreign>
